<p><b>The Coca-Cola Company</b> is  an American corporation, and manufacturer, retailer, and marketer of  nonalcoholic beverage concentrates and <a href="/wiki/Syrup" title="Syrup">syrups</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> The company is best known for its flagship product <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>, invented in 1886 by pharmacist <a href="/wiki/John_Pemberton" title="John Pemberton">John Stith Pemberton</a> in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> The Coca-Cola formula and brand were bought in 1894 by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Asa_Candler" title="Asa Candler">Asa Griggs Candler</a> (December 30, 1851 – March 12, 1929), who incorporated The Coca-Cola Company. The company—headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, but incorporated in Wilmington, Delaware<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup>—has operated a <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchised</a> distribution system since 1889: the Company only produces syrup concentrate, which is then sold to various <a href="/wiki/Bottling_company" title="Bottling company">bottlers</a> throughout the world who hold exclusive territories. The company owns its <a href="/wiki/Anchor_bottler" title="Anchor bottler">anchor bottler</a> in North America, <b>Coca-Cola Refreshments</b>.
The company's stock is listed on the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Stock_Exchange" title="New York Stock Exchange">NYSE</a> and is part of <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">DJIA</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S%26P_500" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a> index, the <a href="/wiki/Russell_1000_Index" title="Russell 1000 Index">Russell 1000 Index</a>, and the Russell 1000 Growth Stock Index. <a href="/wiki/Muhtar_Kent" title="Muhtar Kent">Muhtar Kent</a> serves as chairman of the company with <a href="/wiki/James_Quincey" title="James Quincey">James Quincey</a> as president and chief executive officer.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a></div><p>In 1886, pharmacist John Pemberton invented the original Coca-Cola drink and sold it as a medicinal beverage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">[5]</a></sup> Pemberton's bookkeeper, Frank M. Robinson is credited naming the products and creating its logo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> Robinson chose the name Coca-Cola because of its two main ingredients (coca leaves and kola nuts) and because it sounded like an alliteration. John Pemberton had taken a break and left Robinson to make, promote as well as sell Coca-Cola on his own. He promoted the drink the best he could with the limited budget that he had and succeeded.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1894, American businessman Asa Candler purchased the company from Pemberton's heirs with the intent to advertise and sell it as a beverage to regular consumers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">[5]</a></sup> Candler was one of the first businessmen to use merchandising in his advertising strategy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-5">[5]</a></sup> By 1895, Coca-Cola was being sold in every state in the union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8">[8]</a></sup> Coca-Cola’s first ad read "Coca Cola. Delicious! Refreshing! Exhilarating! Invigorating!"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-7">[7]</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 1948, Coca-Cola had claimed about 60% of the market share.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8">[8]</a></sup> In 1919, the company was sold to Ernest Woodruff's Trust Company of Georgia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> By 1984, The Coca-Cola Company's market share decreased to 21.8% due to new competitors, namely Pepsi, being released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acquisitions">Acquisitions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Acquisitions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The company has a long history of acquisitions. Coca-Cola acquired <a href="/wiki/Minute_Maid" title="Minute Maid">Minute Maid</a> in 1960<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> and in 1982, it acquired the movie studio <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Columbia Pictures</a> for $692 million but was sold to <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a> for $3 billion in 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sellers19971013_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-sellers19971013-11">[11]</a></sup> It acquired the Indian cola brand <a href="/wiki/Thums_Up" title="Thums Up">Thums Up</a> in 1993,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Barq%27s" title="Barq's">Barq's</a> in 1995.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In 2001, it acquired the <a href="/wiki/Odwalla" title="Odwalla">Odwalla</a> brand of fruit juices, smoothies, and bars for $181 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coca-Cola-Oct-2001-SC-TO-T_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coca-Cola-Oct-2001-SC-TO-T-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> In 2007, it acquired <a href="/wiki/Fuze_Beverage" title="Fuze Beverage">Fuze Beverage</a> from founder Lance Collins and Castanea Partners for an estimated $250 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coca-Cola-Feb-2007-10-K_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coca-Cola-Feb-2007-10-K-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> The company's 2009 bid to buy a Chinese juice maker ended when China rejected its $2.4 billion bid for the <a href="/wiki/Huiyuan_Juice" title="Huiyuan Juice">Huiyuan Juice Group</a>, on the grounds the resulting company would be a virtual monopoly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Coca-Cola-Apr-2009-10-Q_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-Coca-Cola-Apr-2009-10-Q-18">[18]</a></sup> Nationalism was also thought to be a reason for aborting the deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2011, it acquired the remaining stake in <a href="/wiki/Honest_Tea" title="Honest Tea">Honest Tea</a>, having bought a 40% stake in 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> In 2013, it finalized its purchase of <a href="/wiki/ZICO_(beverage)" title="ZICO (beverage)">ZICO</a>, a coconut water company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In August 2014, it acquired a 16.7% stake in <a href="/wiki/Monster_Beverage" title="Monster Beverage">Monster Beverage</a> for $2.15 billion with an option to increase it to 25%, as part of a long-term strategic partnership that includes marketing and distribution alliance, and product line swap.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MonsterCoke_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-MonsterCoke-24">[24]</a></sup> In 2015, the company took a minority stake ownership in the cold pressed juice manufacturer, Suja Life LLC.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> In December 2016, it bought many of the former <a href="/wiki/SABMiller" title="SABMiller">SABMiller</a>'s Coca-Cola operations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> On 31 August 2018, it agreed to acquire <a href="/wiki/Costa_Coffee" title="Costa Coffee">Costa Coffee</a> from <a href="/wiki/Whitbread" title="Whitbread">Whitbread</a> for £3.9bn and is expected to go through in the first half of 2019.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Revenue_and_sales">Revenue and sales</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Revenue and sales">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1703" data-file-width="2058" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG/220px-CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG/330px-CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG/440px-CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CocaColaSugarLandTX.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Coca-Cola Company's Minute Maid group North America offices in <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Land_Town_Square" title="Sugar Land Town Square">Sugar Land Town Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sugar_Land,_Texas" title="Sugar Land, Texas">Sugar Land, Texas</a>, United States</div></div></div>
<p>According to The Coca-Cola Company's 2005 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Annual_Report" title="Annual Report">Annual Report</a>, the firm at that time sold beverage products in more than 200 countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archivesa_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-archivesa-29">[29]</a></sup> The 2005 report further states that of the more than 50 billion beverage servings of all types consumed worldwide, daily, beverages bearing the trademarks owned by or licensed to Coca-Cola account for approximately 1.5 billion. Of these, beverages bearing the trademark "<a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a>" or "Coke" accounted for approximately 78% of the company's total gallon sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-archivesa_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-archivesa-29">[29]</a></sup> According to the 2007 Annual Report, Coca-Cola had gallon sales distributed as follows: 43% in the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, 37% in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>, <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">Brazil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/China" title="China">People's Republic of China</a>, and 20% spread throughout the rest of the world.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The figure in 2010 showed that they sold 1.6 billion drinks every day.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>In 2010, it was announced that Coca-Cola had become the first brand to top £1 billion in annual UK grocery sales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Edinburgh_Evening_News_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Edinburgh_Evening_News-30">[30]</a></sup> In 2017, Coke sales were down 11% from a year ago due to consumer tastes shifting away from sugary drinks and due to health risks associated with artificial sweeteners in diet drinks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sales_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-sales-31">[31]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Stock">Stock</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Stock">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coca_Cola_1929.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2463" data-file-width="3242" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coca_Cola_1929.JPG/220px-Coca_Cola_1929.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coca_Cola_1929.JPG/330px-Coca_Cola_1929.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/Coca_Cola_1929.JPG/440px-Coca_Cola_1929.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coca_Cola_1929.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Certificate of Purchase Class A Stock for 20 Shares of The Coca-Cola Company, issued 20. February 1929</div></div></div>
<p>Since the 1920s, Coca-Cola has been a publicly traded company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> One share of stock purchased in 1919 for $40, with all dividends reinvested, would be worth $9.8 million in 2012, a 10.7% annual increase, adjusted for inflation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 1987, Coca-Cola once again became one of the 30 stocks which makes up the <a href="/wiki/Dow_Jones_Industrial_Average" title="Dow Jones Industrial Average">Dow Jones Industrial Average</a>, which is commonly referenced as a proxy for stock market performance; it had previously been a Dow stock from 1932 to 1935.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Coca-Cola has paid a dividend, increasing each year for 49 years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Stock is available from a <a href="/wiki/Dividend_reinvestment_plan" title="Dividend reinvestment plan">direct purchase program</a>, through Computershare Trust Company, but unlike many programs, has investment fees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Staff_and_management">Staff and management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Staff and management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Bottlers">Bottlers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bottlers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:102px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4174" data-file-width="2354" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg/100px-15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg/150px-15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg/200px-15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg 2x" width="100"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:15-09-26-RalfR-WLC-0098.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coca-Cola</div></div></div>
<p>In general, The Coca-Cola Company and its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Subsidiaries" title="Subsidiaries">subsidiaries</a> only produce <a href="/wiki/Syrup" title="Syrup">syrup</a> concentrate, which is then sold to various <a href="/wiki/Bottling_company" title="Bottling company">bottlers</a> throughout the world who hold a local Coca-Cola <a href="/wiki/Franchising" title="Franchising">franchise</a>. Coca-Cola bottlers, who hold territorially exclusive contracts with the company, produce the finished product in cans and bottles from the concentrate, in combination with filtered water and sweeteners. The bottlers then sell, distribute, and merchandise the resulting Coca-Cola product to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Retail_store" title="Retail store">retail stores</a>, vending machines, restaurants, and food service distributors. Outside the United States, these bottlers also control the fountain business.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Since the early 1980s, the company has actively encouraged the consolidation of bottlers, with the company often owning a share of these "anchor bottlers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Outside North America</dt></dl>
<p>The company's largest bottlers outside North America are:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-largest_bottlers_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-largest_bottlers-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Amatil" title="Coca-Cola Amatil">Coca-Cola Amatil</a>, based in Australia (Australia, New Zealand, Indonesia, South Pacific nations) (Company owns a share)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_European_Partners" title="Coca-Cola European Partners">Coca-Cola European Partners PLC</a>, based in the United Kingdom (western Europe) (Company owns share)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_Beverages_Pvt._Ltd." title="International Beverages Pvt. Ltd.">International Beverages Pvt. Ltd.</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Bangladesh" title="Bangladesh">Bangladesh</a> (Fully owned subsidiary of The Coca Cola Company) <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottling_Shqip%C3%ABria" title="Coca-Cola Bottling Shqipëria">Coca-Cola Bottling Shqipëria</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">Albania</a></li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottlers_Philippines,_Inc." title="Coca-Cola Bottlers Philippines, Inc.">Coca-Cola Bottlers Philippines, Inc.</a>, based in the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, a joint venture between the company and <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_FEMSA" title="Coca-Cola FEMSA">Coca-Cola FEMSA</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_FEMSA" title="Coca-Cola FEMSA">Coca-Cola FEMSA</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> (parts of Mexico and Latin America) (Company owns share)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arca_Continental" title="Arca Continental">Arca Continental</a>, also based in Mexico (parts of Mexico and Latin America and in US under Coca-Cola Southwest Beverages LLC in the state of Texas and parts of New Mexico, Oklahoma and Arkansas ) (independent)</li>
<li><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Embotelladora_Andina_S.A&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Embotelladora Andina S.A (page does not exist)">Embotelladora Andina S.A</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> (southern South America) (independent)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Beverages_Africa" title="Coca-Cola Beverages Africa">Coca-Cola Beverages Africa</a>, based in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Port_Elizabeth,_South_Africa" title="Port Elizabeth, South Africa">Port Elizabeth, South Africa</a> (southern and eastern Africa) (company owns share)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Korea" title="Coca-Cola Korea">Coca-Cola Korea</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (independent)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_HBC_AG" title="Coca-Cola HBC AG">Coca-Cola HBC AG</a>, originally based in <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a> but now located in <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a> (Greece, Ireland, Eastern Europe, Russia, and Nigeria) (Company owns share)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Icecek" title="Coca-Cola Icecek">Coca-Cola Icecek</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> (Turkey, southwest Asia, Arabia) (Company owns share)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swire_Group" title="Swire Group">Swire Group</a>, based in Hong Kong (China, Taiwan, Hong Kong) (independent)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Kirin_Company" title="Kirin Company">Kirin Company</a>, based in Japan (independent)</li></ul>
<dl><dt>In the United States</dt></dl>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1704" data-file-width="2272" height="150" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG/200px-CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG/300px-CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG/400px-CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CocaColaBottlingHouston.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Houston Coca-Cola Bottling Company</div></div></div>
<p>In the United States, the company bypasses bottlers and is responsible for the manufacture and sale of fountain syrups directly to authorized fountain wholesalers and some fountain retailers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>After purchasing the North American assets of <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Enterprises" title="Coca-Cola Enterprises">Coca-Cola Enterprises</a>, as of 2014 the company directly owns 100% of Coca-Cola Refreshments, the anchor bottler of Coca-Cola products in North America, representing about 90% of Canada and 80% of the United States.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p><p>Other major bottlers in the United States are:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottling_Co._Consolidated" title="Coca-Cola Bottling Co. Consolidated">Coca-Cola Bottling Co. Consolidated</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a> (company owns share)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottling_Company_of_Northern_New_England" title="Coca-Cola Bottling Company of Northern New England">Coca-Cola Bottling Company of Northern New England</a> based in <a href="/wiki/Bedford,_New_Hampshire" title="Bedford, New Hampshire">Bedford, New Hampshire</a> and owned by Kirin Company</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_Bottling_Company_United" title="Coca-Cola Bottling Company United">Coca-Cola Bottling Company United</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Birmingham,_Alabama" title="Birmingham, Alabama">Birmingham, Alabama</a> (independent)</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swire_Group" title="Swire Group">Swire Coca-Cola USA</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City" title="Salt Lake City">Salt Lake City</a>, Utah and owned by Swire Group</li></ul>
<p>In September 2015, the company announced the sale of several production plants and territories to Swire, Consolidated, and United, and creation of the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Coca-Cola_National_Product_Supply_System&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Coca-Cola National Product Supply System (page does not exist)">Coca-Cola National Product Supply System</a> which controls 95% of the territory in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_relations_and_civic_involvement">Consumer relations and civic involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Consumer relations and civic involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>After <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Martin_Luther_King,_Jr." title="Martin Luther King, Jr.">Martin Luther King, Jr.</a> won the 1964 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Peace_Prize" title="Nobel Peace Prize">Nobel Peace Prize</a>, plans for an interracial celebratory dinner in still-<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Segregated_Atlanta" title="Segregated Atlanta">segregated Atlanta</a> were not initially well supported by the city's business elite until Coca-Cola intervened.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p><a href="/wiki/J._Paul_Austin" title="J. Paul Austin">J. Paul Austin</a>, the chairman and CEO of Coca-Cola, and Mayor Ivan Allen summoned key Atlanta business leaders to the Commerce Club's eighteenth floor dining room, where Austin told them flatly, 'It is embarrassing for Coca-Cola to be located in a city that refuses to honor its Nobel Prize winner. We are an international business. The Coca-Cola Company does not need Atlanta. You all need to decide whether Atlanta needs the Coca-Cola Company.' Within two hours of the end of that meeting, every ticket to the dinner was sold.</p><div class="templatequotecite">— <cite><a href="/wiki/Andrew_Young" title="Andrew Young">Andrew Young</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Young_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Young-45">[45]</a></sup></cite></div>
</blockquote>
<p>Throughout 2012, Coca-Cola contributed $1,700,500 to a $46 million political campaign known as "The Coalition Against The Costly Food Labeling Proposition, sponsored by Farmers and Food Producers".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> This organization was set up to oppose a citizen's initiative, known as Proposition 37, demanding mandatory labeling of foods containing genetically modified ingredients.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Prop_37_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Prop_37-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2012, Coca-Cola was listed as a partner of the <a href="/wiki/Product_Red" title="Product Red">(RED)</a> campaign, together with other brands such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nike,_Inc" title="Nike, Inc">Nike</a>, <a href="/wiki/Girl_Distribution_Company" title="Girl Distribution Company">Girl</a>, <a href="/wiki/American_Express" title="American Express">American Express</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Converse_(shoe_company)" title="Converse (shoe company)">Converse</a>. The campaign's mission is to prevent the transmission of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_immunodeficiency_virus" title="Human immunodeficiency virus">HIV virus</a> from mother to child by 2015 (the campaign's byline is "Fighting for an AIDS Free Generation").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Coca-Cola" title="Criticism of Coca-Cola">Criticism of Coca-Cola</a></div>
<p>Since the early 2000s, the criticisms over the use of Coca-Cola products as well as the company itself, escalated with concerns over health effects, environmental issues, <a href="/wiki/Animal_testing" title="Animal testing">animal testing</a>, economic business practices and employee issues. The Coca-Cola Company has been faced with multiple lawsuits concerning these various criticisms.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising">Advertising</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Advertising">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1401" data-file-width="2086" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg/200px-%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg/300px-%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg/400px-%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%2796-%2702_Chevrolet_Express_Wagon_Coca-Cola.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet_Express" title="Chevrolet Express">Chevrolet Express</a> van bearing the logo of The Coca-Cola Company.</div></div></div>
<p>Coca-Cola advertising has "been among the most prolific in marketing history", with a notable and major impact on popular culture and society as a whole.
</p><p>The logo, bottle design, and brand image are internationally recognizable. Their product is ranked the number one soft drink, repeatedly, internationally, and has notoriety as the first soft drink consumed by astronauts in space. Coca-Cola employs a diverse range of integrated marketing communications to advertise through direct marketing, web based media, social media, and sales promotions (Stringer, 2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p><p>The company carefully considers all touch points a consumer (or <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Prospective_consumer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Prospective consumer (page does not exist)">prospective consumer</a>) has with the brand as potential delivery channels for the brand's message, and makes use of all relevant communication systems. This well established, long-standing, consistent approach has created a longing for the product that by far "superseded the desire for that typically associated with a drink to quench one's thirst" (Dudovskiy, 2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Direct marketing</dt></dl>
<p>They have exclusive vendor company partnerships, which eliminates competition, e.g. cinemas and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Restaurants" title="Restaurants">restaurants</a> only serving Coca-Cola over <a href="/wiki/Pepsi" title="Pepsi">Pepsi</a>. At sponsored sporting events, they again eliminate competition by attaining sole sale rights as well as VIP sales opportunities to important clients, for example, <a href="/wiki/Baseball_field" title="Baseball field">baseball fields</a>.
</p>
<dl><dt>Viral marketing</dt></dl>
<p>The company also markets via mobile marketing in text messages, e.g. viral marketing campaigns (Stringer, 2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-1"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Web and social media</dt></dl>
<p>They set the industry benchmark as the brand so universally recognized that audience building is unnecessary. Their fan engagement spans 86 million globally across social media channels. They deliver a consistently unified message whether it be through new products, online interaction, and social, cultural, or sporting events (Stringer, 2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-2"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<dl><dt>Sales and promotions</dt></dl>
<p>In the retail setting, direct store beverage delivery trucks (mobile advertising) as well as point of sale coolers and vending machines have bright red logo blazoned branding. In terms of food service, Coca-Cola is a food pairing suggestion that is now ingrained as a food match, e.g., for popcorn, burgers, fries, and hot dog combos (Stringer, 2015).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_49-3"><a href="#cite_note-:0-49">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_brands">Products and brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Products and brands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Coca-Cola_brands" title="List of Coca-Cola brands">List of Coca-Cola brands</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_assets_owned_by_The_Coca-Cola_Company" title="List of assets owned by The Coca-Cola Company">List of assets owned by The Coca-Cola Company</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Coca-Cola_offices_(Madrid,_Spain)_04.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1425" data-file-width="2391" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg/220px-Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg/330px-Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg/440px-Coca-Cola_offices_%28Madrid%2C_Spain%29_04.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Coca-Cola_offices_(Madrid,_Spain)_04.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Coca-Cola Company's office building in <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> (Spain)</div></div></div>
<p>The Coca-Cola Company offers more than 350 brands in over 200 countries, aside from its namesake <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola" title="Coca-Cola">Coca-Cola</a> beverage.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Non-food_assets">Non-food assets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Non-food assets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Columbia_Pictures">Columbia Pictures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Columbia Pictures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Coca-Cola bought <a href="/wiki/Columbia_Pictures" title="Columbia Pictures">Columbia Pictures</a> in 1981 owing to the low monetary value of the studio. The film company was the first and only studio ever owned by Coca-Cola. During its ownership of the studio, the studio released many popular films including <i><a href="/wiki/Ghostbusters" title="Ghostbusters">Ghostbusters</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Stripes_(film)" title="Stripes (film)">Stripes</a></i>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Karate_Kid_(1984_film)" title="The Karate Kid (1984 film)">The Karate Kid</a></i>, and some others. However, after the 1987 film <i><a href="/wiki/Ishtar_(film)" title="Ishtar (film)">Ishtar</a></i>, Columbia was sold to Tokyo-based <a href="/wiki/Sony" title="Sony">Sony</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="World_of_Coca-Cola">World of Coca-Cola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: World of Coca-Cola">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/World_of_Coca-Cola" title="World of Coca-Cola">World of Coca-Cola</a></div>
<p>Coca-Cola operates a soft drink themed tourist attraction in Atlanta, Georgia; the <a href="/wiki/World_of_Coca-Cola" title="World of Coca-Cola">World of Coca-Cola</a> is a multi-storied exhibition. It features flavor sampling and a history museum, with locations in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Las_Vegas,_Nevada" title="Las Vegas, Nevada">Las Vegas, Nevada</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lake_Buena_Vista,_Florida" title="Lake Buena Vista, Florida">Lake Buena Vista, Florida</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_of_Coca-Cola_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-World_of_Coca-Cola-51">[51]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rolling_Out_-_World_of_Coca-Cola_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rolling_Out_-_World_of_Coca-Cola-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brands">Brands</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Brands">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_soft_drinks">Other soft drinks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Other soft drinks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Coca-Cola Company also produces a number of other soft drinks including <a href="/wiki/Fanta" title="Fanta">Fanta</a> (introduced circa 1941) and <a href="/wiki/Sprite_(soft_drink)" title="Sprite (soft drink)">Sprite</a>. Fanta's origins date back to World War II during a trade embargo against Germany on cola syrup, making it impossible to sell Coca-Cola in Germany. <a href="/wiki/Max_Keith" title="Max Keith">Max Keith</a>, the head of Coca-Cola's German office during the war, decided to create a new product for the German market, made from products only available in Germany at the time, which they named Fanta.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> The drink proved to be a hit, and when Coke took over again after the war, it adopted the Fanta brand as well. Fanta was originally an orange flavored soft drink which can come in <a href="/wiki/Plastic_bottle" title="Plastic bottle">plastic bottles</a> or cans. It has become available in many different flavors now such as grape, peach, grapefruit, apple, pineapple, and strawberry.
</p><p>In 1961, Coca-Cola introduced Sprite, a lemon-lime soft drink, and another of the company's bestsellers and its response to <a href="/wiki/7_Up" title="7 Up">7 Up</a>.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tab_(soft_drink)" title="Tab (soft drink)">Tab</a> was Coca-Cola's first attempt to develop a diet soft drink, using <a href="/wiki/Saccharin" title="Saccharin">saccharin</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Sugar_substitute" title="Sugar substitute">sugar substitute</a>. Introduced in 1963, the product is still sold today, although its sales have dwindled since the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Diet_Coke" title="Diet Coke">Diet Coke</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tab_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-tab-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="1536" height="293" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg/220px-Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg/330px-Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg/440px-Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Last_Minute_Refreshment.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An ad in Berlin, Germany.</div></div></div>
<p>Coca-Cola South Africa also released <a href="/wiki/Valpre" title="Valpre">Valpre</a> Bottled "still" and "sparkling" water.
</p><p>In 1969, the company released Simba, which was a take on Mountain Dew, and had packaging that was African desert themed, replete with an African Lion as the symbol of the brand.  The tagline was "Simba – It Cures the African Thirst."
</p><p>Also in 1969, the company released a line of products under the name of Santiba, which was targeted for mixing cocktails and party usage, products including Quinine water and Ginger Ale.  Like the above-mentioned Simba, the Santiba line of products was short lived in the marketplace.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="BreakMate">BreakMate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: BreakMate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/BreakMate" title="BreakMate">BreakMate</a></div>
<p>No longer manufactured, the Coca-Cola BreakMate was a three-flavour dispenser introduced by Coca-Cola and <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a> in 1988. Intended for use in offices with five to fifty people,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> its refrigerated compartment held three individual one-litre plastic containers of soda syrup and a CO<sub>2</sub> tank. Like a soda fountain, it mixed syrup in a 1:5 ratio with carbonated water. In North America, Coca-Cola discontinued spare BreakMate parts in 2007 and stopped distributing the syrup in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthy_beverages">Healthy beverages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Healthy beverages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>During the 1990s, the company responded to the growing consumer interest in healthy beverages by introducing several new non-carbonated beverage brands. These included <a href="/wiki/Minute_Maid" title="Minute Maid">Minute Maid</a> Juices to Go, <a href="/wiki/Powerade" title="Powerade">Powerade</a> sports beverage, flavored tea <a href="/wiki/Nestea" title="Nestea">Nestea</a> (in a joint venture with <a href="/wiki/Nestl%C3%A9" title="Nestlé">Nestlé</a>), <a href="/wiki/Fruitopia" title="Fruitopia">Fruitopia</a> fruit drink, and <a href="/wiki/Dasani" title="Dasani">Dasani</a> water, among others. In 2001, the Minute Maid division launched the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Simply_Orange" title="Simply Orange">Simply Orange</a> brand of juices including <a href="/wiki/Orange_juice" title="Orange juice">orange juice</a>. In 2016, <a href="/wiki/Coca-Cola_India" title="Coca-Cola India">Coca-Cola India</a> introduced <a href="/wiki/Vio_(flavoured_milk)" title="Vio (flavoured milk)">Vio (flavoured milk)</a> to enter into the value-added <a href="/wiki/Dairy_product" title="Dairy product">dairy</a> category. The product lays the foundation for Coca-Cola's new segment after <a href="/wiki/Soft_drink" title="Soft drink">carbonated beverages</a>, water and juices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, perhaps in response to the burgeoning popularity of <a href="/wiki/Low-carbohydrate_diet" title="Low-carbohydrate diet">low-carbohydrate diets</a> such as the <a href="/wiki/Atkins_diet" title="Atkins diet">Atkins diet</a>, Coca-Cola announced its intention to develop and sell a low-carbohydrate alternative to Coke Classic, dubbed <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C2_Cola" title="C2 Cola">C2 Cola</a>. C2 contains a mix of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High_fructose_corn_syrup" title="High fructose corn syrup">high fructose corn syrup</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aspartame" title="Aspartame">aspartame</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sucralose" title="Sucralose">sucralose</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Acesulfame_potassium" title="Acesulfame potassium">Acesulfame potassium</a>. C2 is designed to more closely emulate the taste of Coca-Cola Classic. Even with less than half of the <a href="/wiki/Food_energy" title="Food energy">food energy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Carbohydrate" title="Carbohydrate">carbohydrates</a> of standard soft drinks, C2 is not a replacement for zero-calorie soft drinks such as Diet Coke. C2 went on sale in the U.S. on June 11, 2004, and in Canada in August 2004. C2's future is uncertain due to disappointing sales.
</p><p>Starting in 2009, The Coca-Cola Company invested in <a href="/wiki/Innocent_Drinks" title="Innocent Drinks">Innocent Drinks</a>, first with a minor stake, increasing to 90% in the first quarter of 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ccc_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-ccc-58">[58]</a></sup>
</p><p>It was in May 2014 when Finley, a sparkling fruit-flavoured drink, was launched in France. It was launched in other countries later,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaa_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-aaa-59">[59]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Luxembourg" title="Luxembourg">Luxembourg</a> in September 2014. Coca-cola first started developing the drink in Belgium in 2001.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbb_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbb-60">[60]</a></sup> As of 2014, the drink is targeted for adults, and is low in sugar with four flavors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aaa_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-aaa-59">[59]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Best_selling">Best selling</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Best selling">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Coca-Cola is the best-selling soft drink in most countries, and was recognized as the number one global brand in 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> While the Middle East is one of the only regions in the world where Coca-Cola is not the number one soda drink, Coca-Cola nonetheless holds almost 25% market share (to Pepsi's 75%) and had double-digit growth in 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Similarly, in <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, where the locally produced <a href="/wiki/Irn-Bru" title="Irn-Bru">Irn-Bru</a> was once more popular, 2005 figures show that both Coca-Cola and Diet Coke now outsell Irn-Bru.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">Peru</a>, the native <a href="/wiki/Inca_Kola" title="Inca Kola">Inca Kola</a> has been more popular than Coca-Cola, which prompted Coca-Cola to enter in negotiations with the soft drink's company and buy 50% of its stakes. In Japan, the best selling soft drink is not cola, as (canned) <a href="/wiki/Canned_tea" title="Canned tea">tea</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Japanese_canned_coffee" title="Japanese canned coffee">coffee</a> are more popular.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> As such, The Coca-Cola Company's best selling brand there is not Coca-Cola, but <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Georgia_(drink)" title="Georgia (drink)">Georgia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> In May 2016, The Coca-Cola Company temporarily halted production of its signature drink in <a href="/wiki/Venezuela" title="Venezuela">Venezuela</a> due to sugar shortages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Since then, The Coca-Cola Company has since been using "minimum inventories of raw material" to make their signature drinks at two production plants in Venezuela.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Information">Information</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Information">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On July 6, 2006, a Coca-Cola employee and two other people were arrested and charged with trying to sell trade secrets information to the soft drink maker's competitor, <a href="/wiki/PepsiCo" title="PepsiCo">PepsiCo</a> for $1.5 million. The recipe for Coca-Cola, perhaps the company's most closely guarded secret, was never in jeopardy. Instead, the information was related to a new beverage in development. Coca-Cola executives verified that the documents were valid and proprietary. At least one glass vial containing a sample of a new drink was offered for sale, court documents said. The conspiracy was revealed by PepsiCo, which notified the authorities when they were approached by the conspirators.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Green_tea">Green tea</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Green tea">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The company announced a new "negative <a href="/wiki/Calorie" title="Calorie">calorie</a>" green tea drink, <a href="/wiki/Enviga" title="Enviga">Enviga</a>, in 2006, along with trying coffee retail concepts <a href="/wiki/Far_Coast" title="Far Coast">Far Coast</a> and <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chaqwa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chaqwa (page does not exist)">Chaqwa</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Glaceau">Glaceau</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Glaceau">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On May 25, 2007, Coca-Cola announced it would purchase <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glaceau" title="Glaceau">Glaceau</a>, a maker of flavored vitamin-enhanced drinks (vitamin water), flavored waters, and <a href="/wiki/Burn_(energy_drink)" title="Burn (energy drink)">Burn</a> energy drinks, for $4.1 billion in cash.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TCCC-Glaceau_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-TCCC-Glaceau-69">[69]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Huiyuan_Juice">Huiyuan Juice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Huiyuan Juice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>On September 3, 2008, Coca-Cola announced its intention to make cash offers to purchase <a href="/wiki/Huiyuan_Juice" title="Huiyuan Juice">China Huiyuan Juice Group Limited</a> (which has a 42% share of the Chinese pure fruit juice market<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup>) for US$2.4bn (HK$12.20 per share).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> China's <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Commerce_of_the_People%27s_Republic_of_China" title="Ministry of Commerce of the People's Republic of China">ministry of commerce</a> blocked the deal on March 18, 2009, arguing that the deal would hurt small local juice companies, could have pushed up juice market prices, and limited consumers' choices.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Coke_Mini_can">Coke Mini can</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Coke Mini can">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In October 2009, Coca-Cola revealed its new 90-calorie <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Coke_mini" title="Coke mini">mini can</a> that holds 7.5 fluid ounces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cokemini_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-cokemini-73">[73]</a></sup> The mini can is often sold in 8 packs. Despite costing nearly 30 percent more per ounce, the mini cans have been met with positive sales figures.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Holiday_can">Holiday can</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Holiday can">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In November 2011, Coca-Cola revealed a seasonal design for their regular Coke cans as part of a partnership with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/World_Wild_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wild Fund for Nature">World Wildlife Fund</a>. However it was withdrawn only a month after release due to consumer complaints about the similar look to the silver cans commonly used for Diet Coke. There were also complaints about deviating from traditional red as the color of Coca-Cola cans previously.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Stake_in_Monster_Beverage">Stake in Monster Beverage</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Stake in Monster Beverage">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>It was announced on August 14, 2014, that Coca-Cola Co is making a cash payment of $2.15 billion for a 16.7 percent stake in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Monster_Beverage_Corp" title="Monster Beverage Corp">Monster Beverage Corp</a> to expand its market for energy drinks. Coke's ownership in <a href="/wiki/Full_Throttle_(drink)" title="Full Throttle (drink)">Full Throttle</a> and Burn will be transferred to Monster. In return, Monster will transfer its ownership in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hansen_Natural" title="Hansen Natural">Hansen's Natural Sodas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Peace_Iced_Tea" title="Peace Iced Tea">Peace Iced Tea</a> to Coke. <a href="/wiki/Muhtar_Kent" title="Muhtar Kent">Muhtar Kent</a>, Coke's chief executive officer, stated that the company has the option to increase its stake to 25 percent but cannot exceed that percentage in the next four years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ATHAVALEY-Monster_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-ATHAVALEY-Monster-76">[76]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gelles-Monster_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gelles-Monster-77">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sponsorship">Sponsorship</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Sponsorship">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Coca-Cola's advertising expenses accounted for US$3.256 billion in 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Coca-Cola sponsored the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Football_League" title="The Football League">English Football League</a> from the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_in_English_football" title="2004–05 in English football">2004–05 season</a> (beginning August 2004) to the start of 2010/11 season, when the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Football_League" title="Football League">Football League</a> replaced it with <a href="/wiki/Npower_(United_Kingdom)" title="Npower (United Kingdom)">NPower</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Along with this, Coca-Cola sponsored the Coca-Cola Football Camp, that took place in Pretoria, South Africa during the <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">2010 FIFA World Cup</a>, during which hundreds of teenagers from around the world were able to come together and share their love of the game, partly due to <a href="/wiki/Best_Buy" title="Best Buy">Best Buy</a>'s efforts through their @15 program.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>
</p><p>Other major sponsorships include the <a href="/wiki/Australian_Football_League" title="Australian Football League">AFL</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NHRA" title="NHRA">NHRA</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASCAR" title="NASCAR">NASCAR</a>, the <a href="/wiki/PGA_Tour" title="PGA Tour">PGA Tour</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NCAA" title="NCAA">NCAA</a> Championships, the <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a>, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NRL" title="NRL">NRL</a>, the <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">FIFA World Cups</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UEFA_European_Championships" title="UEFA European Championships">UEFA European Championships</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The company partnered with <a href="/wiki/Panini_Group" title="Panini Group">Panini</a> to produce the first virtual sticker album for the <a href="/wiki/2006_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2006 FIFA World Cup">2006 FIFA World Cup</a>, and they have collaborated for every World Cup since.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> Each fall, Coca-Cola is the sponsor of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TOUR_Championship" title="TOUR Championship">TOUR Championship</a> by Coca-Cola held at the <a href="/wiki/East_Lake_Golf_Club" title="East Lake Golf Club">East Lake Golf Club</a> in Atlanta, Georgia. The Tour Championship is the season ending tournament of the PGA Tour.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, it has a team in the <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Basketball_Association" title="Philippine Basketball Association">Philippine Basketball Association</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Powerade_Tigers" title="Powerade Tigers">Powerade Tigers</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Television">Television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The company sponsored the popular <a href="/wiki/Fox_Broadcasting_Company" title="Fox Broadcasting Company">Fox</a> singing-competition series <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> from 2002 until 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>Coca-Cola is a sponsor of the nightly talk show on <a href="/wiki/PBS" title="PBS">PBS</a>, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Charlie_Rose,_LLC" title="Charlie Rose, LLC">Charlie Rose</a></i> in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>
</p><p>Coca-Cola are also executive producers of <a href="/wiki/Coke_Studio_(Pakistan)" title="Coke Studio (Pakistan)">Coke Studio (Pakistan)</a>. There are various adaptations of Coke Studio such as <a href="/wiki/Coke_Studio_(India)" title="Coke Studio (India)">Coke Studio (India)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Coke_Studio_(Middle_East)" title="Coke Studio (Middle East)">Coke Studio (Middle East)</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theme_parks">Theme parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Coca-Cola_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Theme parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While not necessarily having naming rights to anything in all locations, the company does sponsor and provide beverages in many theme parks, usually in an exclusive capacity. This includes the <a href="/wiki/Walt_Disney_Parks_and_Resorts" title="Walt Disney Parks and Resorts">Walt Disney Parks and Resorts</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[a]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merlin_Entertainment" title="Merlin Entertainment">Merlin Entertainment</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universal_Parks_%26_Resorts" title="Universal Parks &amp; Resorts">Universal Parks &amp; Resorts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Six_Flags" title="Six Flags">Six Flags</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cedar_Fair" title="Cedar Fair">Cedar Fair</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SeaWorld_Entertainment" title="SeaWorld Entertainment">SeaWorld Entertainment</a> which are six of the nine largest theme park operators worldwide (it is unknown whether OCT Parks China, the Chimelong Group, or Fantawild, the fourth, seventh, and eighth largest theme park operators respectively, use Coca-Cola).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2015_Report_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-2015_Report-86">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>The company also directly sponsors, with naming rights, the Coca-Cola <a href="/wiki/London_Eye" title="London Eye">London Eye</a> and the Coca-Cola <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orlando_Eye" title="Orlando Eye">Orlando Eye</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orlando_Eye_1_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Orlando_Eye_1-87">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Orlando_Eye_2_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Orlando_Eye_2-88">[87]</a></sup>
</p><p>The company also operates "Coca-Cola" visitor centers in Israel, Belgium and Turkey.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cafe.themarker.com_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-cafe.themarker.com-89">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mefik.co.il_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-mefik.co.il-90">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup>
</p>

<ul><li><i><a href="/wiki/Escola_v._Coca-Cola_Bottling_Co." title="Escola v. Coca-Cola Bottling Co.">Escola v. Coca-Cola Bottling Co.</a></i> <span style="font-size:85%;">(1944)</span></li>
